**Proof:** For all  $\mathbf{m} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , a noisy ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^\star \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathsf{Enc}^\star_\mathsf{pk}(\mathbf{m})$  is of the form  $\mathsf{ct}^\star = (\mathbf{Ar}^\star, (\mathbf{SA} + \mathbf{E})\mathbf{r}^\star + \mathbf{e}^\star + \mathbf{m}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa + \ell_2}$ . When  $\mathbf{m} \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , the second part of the ciphertext is uniformly random over  $\mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ . That is, for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , for all pairs  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk})$  in the support of  $\mathsf{Gen}(1^\lambda)$ , the following distributions are identical:  $\{\mathbf{m} \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}, \mathsf{ct}^\star \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}^\star_\mathsf{pk}(\mathbf{m}) : \mathsf{ct}^\star \}$  and  $\{\mathbf{r}^\star \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathcal{D}_\lambda^m, \mathbf{w} \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2} : (\mathbf{Ar}^\star, \mathbf{w}) \}$ . We conclude the proof using the properties of PreImSamp, which imply that the following distributions have statistical distance at most  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :  $\{\mathbf{A} \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa \times m}, \mathbf{r}^\star \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathcal{D}_\lambda^m : (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{Ar}^\star) \}$  and  $\{\mathbf{A} \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa \times m}, \mathbf{u} \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathbb{Z}_N^\kappa : (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{u}) \}$ .

{34}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-34-0"></span>**Proposition 12** (Weak circuit privacy). The LHE presented above satisfies Property 4.6.

**Proof:** For all  $\mathbf{x} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\nu}$ ,  $\mathbf{y} \in [-1, 1]^{\nu \ell_2}$ , we aim at proving the following distributions have statistical distance at most  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\begin{split} \mathcal{D}_0 &= \left\{ \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(1^\lambda), \mathsf{ct} \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mathbf{x}), \mathsf{ct}^\star \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^\star(\mathbf{m}), \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}} = \mathsf{Eval}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}, \mathsf{ct}^\star, \mathbf{y}) : (\mathsf{ct}, \mathsf{ct}^\star, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}}) \end{array} \right. \\ \mathcal{D}_1 &= \left\{ \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(1^\lambda), \mathsf{ct} \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mathbf{x}) \\ \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}} \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^\star(\mu), \mathsf{ct}^\star = \mathsf{Eval}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}}, -\mathbf{y}) : (\mathsf{ct}, \mathsf{ct}^\star, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}}) \end{array} \right\}, \end{split}$$

where  $\mu = (m_1 + \mathbf{x}^{\top} \mathbf{y}_1, \dots, m_{\ell_2} + \mathbf{x}^{\top} \mathbf{y}_{\ell_2}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ .

In distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0$ , we have:

- ct =  $(\mathbf{A}\mathbf{R}, (\mathbf{S}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E})\mathbf{R} + \mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{x}^{\top} \otimes \mathrm{Id}_{\ell_2}),$
- $ct^* = (\mathbf{Ar}^*, (\mathbf{SA} + \mathbf{E}) \mathbf{r}^* + \mathbf{e}^* + \mathbf{x}^*),$
- $\mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{v}} = (\mathbf{A}(\mathbf{R}\mathbf{y} + \mathbf{r}^*), (\mathbf{S}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E})(\mathbf{R}\mathbf{y} + \mathbf{r}^*) + \mathbf{E}'\mathbf{y} + \mathbf{e}^* + \mu).$

We show that it has statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$  from  $\mathcal{D}_1$  by a series of claims.

Claim 1. For all  $\mathbf{y} \in [-1,1]^{\nu \ell_2}$ , the following distributions have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\left\{\mathbf{r}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{m}, \mathbf{R} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-1, 1]^{m \times \nu \ell_{2}} : (\mathbf{R}, \mathbf{r}^{\star}, \mathbf{r}^{\star} + \mathbf{R}\mathbf{y})\right\}$$
$$\left\{\mathbf{r}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{m}, \mathbf{R} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-1, 1]^{m \times \nu \ell_{2}} : (\mathbf{R}, \mathbf{r}^{\star} - \mathbf{R}\mathbf{y}, \mathbf{r}^{\star})\right\},$$

by the properties of PrelmSamp.

Claim 2. For all  $\mathbf{y} \in [-1,1]^{\nu \ell_2}$ , the following distributions have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\left\{ \mathbf{e}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -2^{\lambda}, 2^{\lambda} \right]^{\ell_{2}}, \mathbf{E}' \leftarrow \left[ -2^{\lambda/2}, 2^{\lambda/2} \right]^{\ell_{2} \times \nu \ell_{2}} : \left( \mathbf{E}', \mathbf{e}^{\star}, \mathbf{e}^{\star} + \mathbf{E}' \mathbf{y} \right) \right\} \\
\left\{ \mathbf{e}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -2^{\lambda}, 2^{\lambda} \right]^{\ell_{2}}, \mathbf{E}' \leftarrow \left[ -2^{\lambda/2}, 2^{\lambda/2} \right]^{\ell_{2} \times \nu \ell_{2}} : \left( \mathbf{E}', \mathbf{e}^{\star} - \mathbf{E}' \mathbf{y}, \mathbf{e}^{\star} \right) \right\}.$$

by Lemma 2.2 (smudging).

Claim 1 and Claim 2 imply the following claim.

Claim 3. For all  $\mathbf{y} \in [-1, 1]^{\nu \ell_2}$ , the following distributions have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\mathcal{D}'_{0} = \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \mathbf{e}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -2^{\lambda}, 2^{\lambda} \right]^{\ell_{2}}, \mathbf{E}' \leftarrow \left[ -2^{\lambda/2}, 2^{\lambda/2} \right]^{\ell_{2} \times \nu \ell_{2}}, \mathbf{r}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{m} \\ \mathbf{R} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -1, 1 \right]^{m \times \nu \ell_{2}} : \left( \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{r}^{\star}, \mathbf{r}^{\star} + \mathbf{R}\mathbf{y}, \mathbf{E}', \mathbf{e}^{\star}, \mathbf{e}^{\star} + \mathbf{E}'\mathbf{y} \right) \end{array} \right\}$$

$$\mathcal{D}'_{1} = \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \mathbf{e}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -2^{\lambda}, 2^{\lambda} \right]^{\ell_{2}}, \mathbf{E}' \leftarrow \left[ -2^{\lambda/2}, 2^{\lambda/2} \right]^{\ell_{2} \times \nu \ell_{2}}, \mathbf{r}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{m} \\ \mathbf{R} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -1, 1 \right]^{m \times \nu \ell_{2}} : \left( \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{r}^{\star} - \mathbf{R}\mathbf{y}, \mathbf{r}^{\star}, \mathbf{E}', \mathbf{e}^{\star} - \mathbf{E}'\mathbf{y}, \mathbf{e}^{\star} \right) \end{array} \right\}.$$

Now we prove the following claim, that will conclude the proof of Proposition 12.

{35}------------------------------------------------

Claim 4. There exists a (possibly inefficient) simulator  $\mathcal{S}$  that given as input  $\mathbf{v} \in (\mathbb{Z}_N^{m \times (\nu \ell_2 + 2)}) \times \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2 \times (\nu \ell_2 + 2)}$ , outputs a tuple  $(\mathsf{ct}, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{v}}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{(\kappa + \ell_2) \times \nu \ell_2} \times (\mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa + \ell_2})^2$ , such that when  $\mathcal{S}$  is fed with an input from distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0'$ , it produces an output following the distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0$ , whereas when fed with an input coming from distribution  $\mathcal{D}_1'$ , it produces an output following the distribution  $\mathcal{D}_1$ .

Given as input  $(\mathbf{R}, \mathbf{r}_1, \mathbf{r}_2, \mathbf{E}', \mathbf{e}_1, \mathbf{e}_2)$ ,  $\mathcal{S}$  computes:

- ct =  $(\mathbf{A}\mathbf{R}, (\mathbf{S}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E})\mathbf{R} + \mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{x}^{\top} \otimes \mathrm{Id}_{\ell_2}),$
- $\mathsf{ct}^{\star} = (\mathbf{Ar}_1, (\mathbf{SA} + \mathbf{E}) \mathbf{r}_1 + \mathbf{e}_1 + \mathbf{m}),$
- $ct_y = (Ar_2, (SA + E) r_2 + e_2 + \mu).$

<span id="page-35-0"></span>**Theorem 4.3** (Security). Assume (subexponential) security of the LWE assumption holds. Then, for all polynomials  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ , P-Regev $_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$  is (subexponentially) secure.

**Proof:** In a nutshell, Regev encryption uses the LWE assumption to switch the LWE samples from the public key  $\mathbf{SA} + \mathbf{E}$  to uniformly random, then use the leftover hash lemma to extract the entropy from the randomness used to encrypt the messages. The problem here is that for succinctness, we use small randomness, and large messages: the randomness does not hold enough entropy to hide the messages. Instead, we use the randomness and extra smudging noise to generate fresh LWE samples, and then hide the messages. We now provide the formal proof, which uses the hybrids experiment listed below.

- $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0}$ : as per Definition 2.8. Namely, the experiment generates  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(1^{\lambda})$  where  $\mathsf{pk} = (N, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{SA} + \mathbf{E})$ , sends  $\mathsf{pk}$  to the adversary who chooses a pair  $(\mathbf{x}^{0}, \mathbf{x}^{1}) \in \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\nu_{0}} \times \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\nu_{1}}$  (wlog. we can assume  $\nu_{0} = \nu_{1} = \nu$ ). The experiment samples  $b \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0, 1\}$  and computes the challenge ciphertext as  $\mathsf{ct} = (\mathbf{AR}, (\mathbf{SA} + \mathbf{E})\mathbf{R} + \mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{x}^{b} \otimes \mathsf{Id}_{\ell_{2}})$ , which is sent to the adversary, who wins if it guesses b successfully.
- $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1}$ : this experiment is the same as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0}$  except the challenge ciphertext is now of the form  $\mathsf{ct} = (\mathbf{AR}, \mathbf{SAR} + \mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{x}^b \otimes \mathrm{Id}_{\ell_2})$ . Recall that  $\mathbf{E} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \chi^{\ell_2 \times m}$  where  $\chi$  is  $B_{\chi}$ -bounded, for a polynomial  $B_{\chi}$ ,  $\mathbf{R} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-1,1]^{m \times \ell_2}$  for a polynomial m and  $\mathbf{E}' \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-2^{\lambda/2},2^{\lambda/2}]^{\ell_2 \times \ell_2}$ . Thus, we can use Lemma 2.2 (smudging) to argue that  $\mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{ER} \approx_s \mathbf{E}'$  with statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ . The first distribution corresponds to  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0}$  (with pre and post-processing), whereas the second distribution corresponds to  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1}$  (with pre and post-processing).
- $\underline{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^2}$ : this experiment is the same as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^1$ , except the challenge ciphertext is now of the form  $\mathsf{ct} = (\mathbf{U}, \mathbf{S}\mathbf{U} + \mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{x}^b \otimes \mathrm{Id}_{\ell_2})$ , where  $\mathbf{U} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa \times \ell_2}$ . The fact that  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^1\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^2\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  follows readily from the leftover hash lemma, which states that the following distributions have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\{\mathbf{A} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\kappa \times m}, \mathbf{R} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-1, 1]^{m \times \ell_{2}} : (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{R})\}$$
$$\{\mathbf{A} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\kappa \times m}, \mathbf{U} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\kappa \times \ell_{2}} : (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{U})\}.$$

The first distribution corresponds to  $\mathcal{H}^1_{\lambda}$  (with post-processing), whereas the second distribution corresponds to  $\mathcal{H}^2_{\lambda}$  (with the same post-processing).

•  $\underline{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^3}$ : this experiment is the same as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^2$ , except the challenge ciphertext is now of the form

{36}------------------------------------------------

ct = (**U**, **W**), where  $\mathbf{W} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa \times \nu \ell_2}$ , and the public key is now of the form  $\mathsf{pk} = (N, \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{V})$  where  $\mathbf{V} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2 \times m}$ . We show that  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^2\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^3\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . This holds by the properties of TrapGen, which state that the matrix **A** is statistically close to uniform over  $\mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa \times m}$ . Then, we rely on the LWE assumption, which implies that  $(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{S}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{E}, \mathbf{U}, \mathbf{S}\mathbf{U} + \mathbf{E}' + \mathbf{x}^b \otimes \mathrm{Id}_{\ell_2}) \approx_c (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{V}, \mathbf{U}, \mathbf{W} + \mathbf{x}^b \otimes \mathrm{Id}_{\ell_2}) \equiv (\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{V}, \mathbf{U}, \mathbf{W})$ , where  $\mathbf{W} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa \times \nu \ell_2}$  and  $\mathbf{V} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2 \times m}$ . We conclude by noting that in the experiment  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^3$ , the adversary's view does not depend on the random bit b.

# <span id="page-36-1"></span>5 Constructing XiO for P<sup>log</sup>/poly

We present a modular construction of XiO  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{log}}/\mathsf{poly}$  from the GSW FHE scheme for circuits of depth  $\delta$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$ , for sufficiently sufficiently large  $\delta$ , and any  $(\ell_1, \ell_2, h, \alpha)$ -hintable packed LHE for sufficiently small h,  $\alpha$  and sufficiently large  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ —recall that h measures the LHE succinctness,  $\alpha$  quantifies the approximate correctness, while  $\ell_1$ ,  $\ell_2$  measure the plaintext size, or "batching capacity" of the scheme;  $\ell_1$  intuitively represents how many bits can be packed in a scalar, i.e. how large is the modulus in use, whereas  $\ell_2$  measures how many such scalars are recovered when decrypting one ciphertext. We prove the IND-security of our XiO construction from 2-circular SRL security of the GSW scheme and the hintable LHE.

Outline. In the rest of this section, we abstract out 2 additional properties of the GSW FHE that we will rely on to enable a modular proof. This is done in Section 5.1. Then, we present our XiO construction in Section 5.2. Afterwards, in Section 5.3 we prove the IND-security of our XiO assuming the 2-circular SRL security of the GSW scheme and the hintable LHE. Finally, in Section 5.4 we instantiate our modular construction with Packed-Regev LHE, which yields our main result, namely the existence of XiO (and then iO) from the subexponential LWE assumption and the subexponential 2CIRC conjecture w.r.t. GSW and Packed-Regev LHE. In Appendix A.2 we provide an instantiation with Damgård Jurik LHE encryption.

#### <span id="page-36-0"></span>5.1 Additional properties for GSW

Weak Circuit Privacy of  $GSW_{\delta}$ . As mentionned in the introduction, we will rely on the fact that the GSW encryption scheme also satisfies a notion of "weak circuit privacy" similar to the one defined for LHE. More precisely, we show that GSW satisfies a property that involves a public-key algorithm that re-randomizes evaluated ciphertext so that they look like fresh ciphertexts from the support of the noise encryption algorithm  $Enc^*$ . Namely, we show that there exists a PPT algorithm ReRand that takes as input the public key pk, an evaluated ciphertext ct, some random coins  $r^* \in \mathcal{R}^*$ , and outputs an evaluated ciphertext ct computed as described below.

#### • ReRand( $pk, ct; \mathbf{r}^*$ ):

Given  $\mathsf{pk} = (B, \mathbf{U}, \mathbf{G})$ ,  $\mathsf{ct} \in \{0, 1\}^w$  and  $\mathbf{r}^* \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-B^*, B^*]^m$ , it computes  $\mathsf{ct}' \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$  whose binary decomposition is  $\mathsf{ct}$ , computes  $\widetilde{\mathsf{ct}} = \mathsf{ct}' + \mathbf{Ur}^* \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$ , and outputs the re-randomized ciphertext  $\mathsf{BD}(\widetilde{\mathsf{ct}}) \in \{0, 1\}^w$ .

<span id="page-36-2"></span>**Theorem 5.1** (weak circuit privacy). For all polynomials  $\nu, \ell, \delta$ , all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , all crs containing a modulus  $N \in \mathbb{N}$  such that  $N \geq 2^{2\lambda}B$ , where B is an upper-bound on the noise obtained from homomorphically evaluating circuits of depth at most  $\delta(\lambda)$ , all pairs  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk})$  in the support of  $\mathsf{Gen}(\mathsf{crs})$ , all messages  $\mu \in \{0,1\}^{\nu(\lambda)}$ , all depth- $\delta(\lambda)$  circuits  $f_1, \ldots, f_{\ell(\lambda)} : \{0,1\}^{\nu(\lambda)} \to \mathbb{Z}_N$ , the following

{37}------------------------------------------------

distributions have statistical distance at most  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\mathcal{D}_0: \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \mathsf{ct} \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mu), \forall j \in [\ell(\lambda)], \mathsf{ct}_{f_j} = \mathsf{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, f_j, 0, \mathsf{ct}), \mathbf{r}_j^\star \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathcal{R}^\star \\ \mathsf{ct}_{f_j}^\star = \mathsf{ReRand}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_j}; \mathbf{r}^\star) : \left(\mathsf{ct}, (\mathbf{r}_j^\star, \mathsf{ct}_{f_j}^\star)_{j \in [\ell(\lambda)]}\right) \end{array} \right\} \\ \mathcal{D}_1: \left\{ \begin{array}{l} r \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathcal{R}^{\nu(\lambda)}, \mathsf{ct} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mu; r), \forall j \in [\ell(\lambda)], \mathbf{r}_j^\star \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathcal{R}^\star, \mathsf{ct}_{f_j}^\star = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^\star(f_j(\mu); \mathbf{r}_j^\star) \\ \mathbf{r}_{f_j} = \mathsf{Eval}_\mathsf{rand}\left(\mathsf{pk}, f_j, r, \mu\right) : \left(\mathsf{ct}, (\mathbf{r}_j^\star - \mathbf{r}_{f_j}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_j}^\star)_{j \in [\ell(\lambda)]}\right) \end{array} \right\} \right.$$

**Proof:** By batch correctness of the scheme, for all  $j \in [\ell(\lambda)]$ , the evaluated ciphertext is of the form  $\operatorname{ct}_{f_j} = (\mathbf{A}\mathbf{r}_{f_j}, (\mathbf{s}^{\top}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}^{\top})\mathbf{r}_{f_j} + f_j(\mu)) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$ , and the re-randomized ciphertext is of the form  $\operatorname{ct}_{f_j}^{\star} = (\mathbf{A}(\mathbf{r}_{f_j} + \mathbf{r}_j^{\star}), (\mathbf{s}^{\top}\mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}^{\top})(\mathbf{r}_{f_j} + \mathbf{r}_j^{\star}) + f_j(\mu)) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$ , where  $\|\mathbf{r}_{f_j}\|_{\infty} < (w+1)^{\delta} \lceil \log(N) \rceil = 2^{-\lambda}B^{\star}$  and  $\mathbf{r}_j^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} [-B^{\star}, B^{\star}]^m$ . By Lemma 2.2 (smudging), the following distributions have statistical distance at most  $2^{-\lambda}$ :

$$\left(\mathbf{r}_{j}^{\star}\right)_{j\in\left[\ell\right]}\approx_{s}\left(\mathbf{r}_{j}^{\star}-\mathbf{r}_{f_{j}}\right)_{j\in\left[\ell\right]}.$$

The leftmost distribution corresponds to  $\mathcal{D}_0$  (with pre and post-processing), whereas the rightmost distribution corresponds to  $\mathcal{D}_1$  (with pre and post-processing).

<span id="page-37-2"></span>**Proposition 13**  $(B(2^{\lambda}+1)$ -approximate correctness of refreshed evaluated ciphertexts). For all polynomials  $\nu, \delta$ , all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , all crs containing a large enough modulus  $N \in \mathbb{N}$ , all messages  $\mu \in \{0,1\}^{\nu(\lambda)}$ , all circuits  $f: \{0,1\}^{\nu(\lambda)} \to \mathbb{Z}_N$  of depth at most  $\delta(\lambda)$ , we have:  $\Pr\left[(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(\mathsf{crs}), \mathsf{ct} \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mu), \mathsf{ct}_f = \mathsf{Eval}(\mathsf{pk}, f, 0, \mathsf{ct}), \mathsf{ct}_f' \leftarrow \mathsf{ReRand}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}_f) : |\mathsf{sk}^\top \mathsf{ct}_f' - f(\mu)| \leq B(2^{\lambda} + 1)\right] \in 1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

**Proof:** The ciphertext  $\operatorname{ct}_f$  is the binary decomposition of  $(\mathbf{A}(\mathbf{r}^* + \mathbf{r}_f), (\mathbf{s}^\top \mathbf{A} + \mathbf{e}^\top)(\mathbf{r}^* + \mathbf{r}_f) + f(\mu)) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$ , where  $|\mathbf{e}^\top \mathbf{r}_f| < B$  by batch correctness and  $|\mathbf{e}^\top \mathbf{r}^*| < B_\chi B^* m = 2^\lambda B$  with probability  $1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$  over the choices of  $\mathbf{e} \leftarrow \chi^m$ .

#### <span id="page-37-0"></span>5.2 XiO Construction

We directly dive into the formal description of the construction, see the introduction for a detailed overview.

We present a modular construction of XiO for the class of circuits  $C_{\log(n),s,d}$  for polynomials n, s, d, from the following building blocks:

- the GSW FHE scheme for depth  $\delta$  circuits, denoted by  $GSW_{\delta} = (CRSgen, Gen, Enc, Enc^*, Dec, Eval, Eval', Eval_{rand}, ReRand)$ , presented in Section 3.2.2. The depth  $\delta$  is chosen sufficiently large to handle the homomorphic evaluations of the circuits described below.
- an  $(\ell_1, \ell_2, h, \alpha)$ -Hintable Packed LHE, denoted by  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon} = (\overline{\mathsf{Gen}}, \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}, \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}^{\star}, \overline{\mathsf{Dec}}, \overline{\mathsf{Eval}}, \overline{\mathsf{SecHint}}, \overline{\mathsf{PubHint}}, \overline{\mathsf{Rec}}, \overline{\mathsf{VerKey}})$  where h is independent of n to ensure succinctness;  $\ell_1(\lambda) \geq b(\lambda) + 2\lambda$ , where  $2^b$  is a bound on the noise obtained when FHE evaluating circuits of depth at most  $\delta^{10}$ ; moreover  $(\ell_1(\lambda) b(\lambda) 2\lambda) \cdot \ell_2(\lambda) \geq n^{\varepsilon}(\lambda)$ , where  $\varepsilon \in (0,1)$  is defined below (see the paragraph about succinctness); finally  $\alpha(\lambda) \leq \lambda + 1$ .

<span id="page-37-1"></span>To make sure these parameters are instantiable, we require that LHE decryption is of poly-logarithmic depth, which ensures that  $\delta$  and therefore B only depend poly-logarithmically on  $\ell_1$ .

{38}------------------------------------------------

**Notations.** For every program  $\Pi$  with  $\log(n)$  bits inputs, every  $\varepsilon \in (0,1)$ , the truth table can be written as  $(\Pi_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}$ , where each chunk  $\Pi_i$  contains  $n^{\varepsilon}$  bits. The chunks  $\Pi_i$  themselves can be subdivided into sub-chunks  $\Pi_i = (\Pi_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]}$ , where each sub-chunk  $\Pi_{i,j}$  contains  $n^{\varepsilon}/\ell_2$  bits. For all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$  and  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , we denote by  $C_{i,j}$  the circuit that takes as input a program  $\Pi$  of size s and outputs  $\Pi_{i,j}$ .

The construction: We proceed to the construction.

## $\bullet \ \mathsf{Gen}_{\mathsf{Obf}}(1^{\lambda}) \colon$

Set the parameters:

- Choose a constant  $0 < \varepsilon < 1$  that is small enough so as to ensure succinctness of the scheme (see paragraph succinctness below).
- Let  $|\overline{\mathsf{ct}}|(\cdot)$ ,  $|\overline{\mathbf{r}^{\star}}|(\cdot)$  be polynomials such that for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , every  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}})$  in the support of  $\overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(1^{\lambda})$  that defines the message space  $\mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$  and the noisy randomness space  $\mathcal{R}^{\star}$ , every message  $\mathbf{m} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , every ciphertext in the support of  $\overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{m})$  has a bit size at most  $|\overline{\mathsf{ct}}|(\lambda)$  and every  $\mathbf{r}^{\star} \in \mathcal{R}^{\star}$  has bit size at most  $|\mathbf{r}^{\star}|(\lambda)$ .
- $\bullet \ \ \mathsf{FHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0,1\}^{n^{1-\varepsilon}\cdot \ell_2\cdot |\mathbf{r}^\star|}, \ \mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0,1\}^{n^{1-\varepsilon}\cdot |\overline{\mathsf{ct}}|}.$

Return pp = (FHE.PubCoin, LHE.PubCoin).

## • $\mathsf{Obf}(\mathsf{pp},1^n,\Pi)$ :

Sample the following parameters:

- $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(1^{\lambda})$  that defines the message space  $\mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ .
- $(pk, sk) \leftarrow Gen(\overline{pk})$  that defines the noisy randomness space  $\mathcal{R}^*$ , where  $sk \in \mathbb{Z}_N^w$ , and pk contains the noise bound B; we write  $b = \lceil \log(B) \rceil$ .

Compute the following ciphertexts:

- $\mathsf{ct}_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\Pi)$ .
- $\mathsf{ct}_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}).$
- $\overline{\mathsf{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathsf{sk}).$

For all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]$ , compute the following:

- $\mathsf{ct}_{i,j} = \mathsf{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, C_{i,j}, b + 2\lambda, \mathsf{ct}_1) \in \{0,1\}^w$ , where the circuit  $C_{i,j}$  is defined above. The homomorphic evaluation is performed with scaling factor  $b + 2\lambda$ .
- $\operatorname{ct}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \operatorname{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, f_{i,j}, 0, \operatorname{ct}_2) \in \{0,1\}^w$ , where the circuit  $f_{i,j}$  takes as input a bit string  $\mathbf{a} \in \{0,1\}^{|\overline{\mathsf{sk}}|}$ . It checks that  $\mathbf{a}$  is the secret key associated with  $\overline{\mathsf{pk}}$ , that is, it runs  $\overline{\mathsf{VerKey}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathbf{a})$ . If the latter outputs 0,  $f_{i,j}$  outputs 0. Otherwise, it uses  $\mathbf{a}$  as an LHE secret key to compute  $\mathbf{v}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Dec}}_{\mathbf{a}}(\mathsf{LHE.PubCoin}_i)$ , where  $\mathsf{LHE.PubCoin}_i$  is interpreted as an LHE ciphertext  $\overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{u}_i)$ , with  $\mathbf{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , by density of the LHE ciphertext space. Then it computes  $v_{i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ , the j'th coordinate of  $\mathbf{v}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$  and outputs the most significant bits of  $v_{i,j}$ , of the form:  $\mathsf{MSB}(v_{i,j}) = v_{i,j} \mathsf{LSB}(v_{i,j}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , where the (shifted) least significant bits are of the form:  $\mathsf{LSB}(v_{i,j}) = v_{i,j} \mod B2^{2\lambda} B2^{2\lambda}/2 \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . The homomorphic evaluation is performed with scaling factor 1.

{39}------------------------------------------------

- Parse FHE.PubCoin<sub>i,j</sub> =  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \in \mathcal{R}^{\star}$  and compute  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{ReRand}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}; \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}) \in \mathbb{Z}_{N}^{\kappa+1}$ .
- Compute  $\operatorname{ct}_i = (\operatorname{ct}_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}, \operatorname{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i} = (\operatorname{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}.$
- Compute  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Eval}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_i, \mathsf{ct}_i \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i}).$
- Compute  $\rho_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{SecHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i)$ .

Return  $\widetilde{\Pi} = (\mathsf{pk}, \overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \{\rho_i\}_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}).$ 

- $\bullet$  Eval $(pp,\widetilde{\Pi},\mathbf{x})$ :
  - Let  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$  such that  $\Pi(\mathbf{x})$  belongs to the *i*'th chunk of the truth table of  $\Pi$ . Compute  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i$  as described above.
  - Recover  $m_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Rec}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}_i}, \rho_i)$ .
  - Compute  $m_i' = \lfloor 2^{-2\lambda}/B \cdot m_i \rceil$ , which contains  $\Pi(\mathbf{x})$ .

We now proceed to prove Theorem 5.2.

**Succinctness.** By h-succinctness of  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$ , for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ , we have  $|\rho_i| \leq h(\lambda)$  for a polynomial h that is independent of n. The rest of the obfuscated circuit  $\widetilde{\Pi}$  is of size  $p(\lambda, n^{\varepsilon}, d)$ , for a polynomial p that is independent of n and  $\varepsilon$ . Thus, there exists a constant  $c \in \mathbb{N}$  (independent of  $\varepsilon$ ) and a polynomial q (independent of n) such that  $|\widetilde{\Pi}| \in n^{c\varepsilon}(\lambda) \cdot q(\lambda, d) + n^{1-\varepsilon}(\lambda) \cdot h(\lambda)$ . For succinctness, we pick an appropriately small  $0 < \varepsilon < 1/c$ .

#### Correctness.

• By the batch correctness of the GSW scheme (Proposition 1), for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$  and  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , we have:

$$\mathsf{sk}^{\top}\mathsf{ct}_{i,j} = 2^{2\lambda}B \cdot \Pi_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N,$$

where  $|\mathsf{noise}_{i,j}| < B$ .

- By the density of the noisy ciphertexts of  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$ , for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ , we have LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub> =  $\overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{u}_i)$  with  $\mathbf{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ .
- By the  $(2^{\lambda}+1)B$ -approximate correctness of refreshed evaluated ciphertexts of the GSW scheme (Proposition 13), for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$  and  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , we have:

$$\mathsf{sk}^{\top}\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j}) + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N,$$

where  $|\mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}| < (2^{\lambda} + 1)B$ .

• By linear homomorphism of  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$  (Property 4.2), the ciphertext  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i$  is in the support of  $\overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{m}_i)$ ,  $\mathbf{m}_i = (m_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]}$  of the form:

$$m_{i,j} = B2^{2\lambda} \cdot \Pi_{i,j} + \mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}) + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N.$$

• By  $\alpha$ -correctness of the secret hints of  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$  (Property 4.3), the evaluator of the obfuscated circuit recovers the message  $\overline{\mathbf{m}_i} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$  such that  $\|\overline{\mathbf{m}_i} - \mathbf{m}_i\|_{\infty} < 2^{\alpha(\lambda)}$ . That is, for all  $j \in [\ell_2]$ ,  $\overline{m_{i,j}} = m_{i,j} + \overline{\mathsf{noise}}_{i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ , where  $|\overline{\mathsf{noise}}_{i,j}| < 2^{\alpha(\lambda)}$ .

{40}------------------------------------------------

• With probability  $1 - 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$  over the choice of  $\mathbf{u}_i \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , we have for all  $j \in [\ell_2]$ ,  $|\mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}) + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j}| < B2^{2\lambda}/2$ . Thus,  $m'_{i,j} = \lfloor \overline{m_{i,j}} \cdot 2^{-2\lambda}/B \rfloor = \Pi_{i,j}$  for all  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , and the evaluator outputs  $\Pi(\mathbf{x})$ .

### <span id="page-40-0"></span>5.3 IND Security from 2CIRC

We now state our theorem.

<span id="page-40-1"></span>**Theorem 5.2.** Assume that for all polynomials  $\delta$ , b, all constants  $\varepsilon \in (0,1)$ , there exists a polynomial b s.t. for all polynomials n, there exist polynomials  $\ell_1, \ell_2, \alpha$  and an  $(\ell_1, \ell_2, h, \alpha)$ -hintable packed LHE denoted by  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,\varepsilon,n}$  s.t. for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ :

- $\alpha(\lambda) \le \lambda + 1$
- $\ell_1(\lambda) \geq b(\lambda)$
- $(\ell_1(\lambda) b(\lambda)) \cdot \ell_2(\lambda) > n(\lambda)^{\varepsilon}$
- 2-circular SRL security (resp. subexponential 2-circular SRL security) holds w.r.t.  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,\varepsilon,n}$  and  $GSW_{\delta}$ .

Then  $Xi\mathcal{O}$  (resp. subexponentially secure  $Xi\mathcal{O}$ ) for  $\mathsf{P}^{\log}/\mathsf{poly}$  exists.

**Proof:** We now prove that the XiO scheme presented in Section 5 is IND-secure, provided 2-circular SRL security (as per Definition 3.3) holds w.r.t.  $GSW_{\delta}$  and  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$ .

We proceed via a hybrid argument using the experiments described below for all  $b \in \{0,1\}$  and all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ .

- $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.0}$ : this is the experiment from Definition 2.3. For completeness, we describe it here.
  - Generation of pp: for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ , LHE.PubCoin $_i \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0,1\}^{|\overline{\mathsf{ct}}|}$ , for all  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , FHE.PubCoin $_{i,j} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^*$ , where  $\mathcal{R}^*$  denotes the noisy randomness space of  $\mathcal{FHE}$ . Return  $\mathsf{pp} = \Big((\mathsf{LHE.PubCoin}_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}, (\mathsf{FHE.PubCoin}_{i,j})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]}\Big)$ .
  - Generation of  $\widetilde{\Pi_b}$ :  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(1^{\lambda})$ ,  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}})$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\Pi)$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}})$ ,  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathsf{sk})$ . For all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ ,  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , compute the following:
    - $\operatorname{ct}_{i,j} = \operatorname{Eval}'(\operatorname{pk}, C_{i,j}, b + 2\lambda, \operatorname{ct}_1) \in \{0, 1\}^w;$
    - $\operatorname{ct}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, f_{i,j}, 0, \mathsf{ct}_2) \in \{0,1\}^w;$
    - Parse FHE.PubCoin<sub>i,j</sub> =  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \in \mathcal{R}^{\star}$  and compute  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{ReRand}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}; \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}) \in \{0,1\}^{w}$ .
    - Compute  $\mathsf{ct}_i = (\mathsf{ct}_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}, \ \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i} = (\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}.$
    - $-\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Eval}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_i, \mathsf{ct}_i \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i});$
    - $-\rho_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{SecHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i).$

Return  $\widetilde{\Pi}_b = (\mathsf{pk}, \overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, (\rho_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}).$ 

{41}------------------------------------------------

•  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.1}$ : the experiment samples LHE.PubCoin as in  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.0}$ , but does not sample FHE.PubCoin just yet; it then generates  $\widetilde{\Pi}_b$  as in  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.0}$  up until the point that the  $\mathsf{ct}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}$  get re-randomized into  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}$  via ReRand. Next, instead of performing the re-randomization, it samples  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}$  as a  $\mathit{fresh}$  extra noisy encryption of  $\mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j})$  using randomness  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{\star}$ , and setting FHE.PubCoin<sub>i,j</sub> to be  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} - \mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}}$ , where  $\mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}}$  denotes the evaluated randomness computed via  $\mathsf{Eval}_{\mathsf{rand}}$ . Afterwards, the experiment continues exactly the same way as in the experiment  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.0}$ .

We show that for all  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , we have:

$$\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.0}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.1}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}},$$

using the weak circuit privacy of  $\mathcal{FHE}$  (Theorem 5.1).

The latter states that for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , all  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}})$  in the support of  $\overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(1^{\lambda})$ , all  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk})$  in the support of  $\overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}})$ , for all depth d-circuits and in particular the functions  $f_{i,j}$  defined previously, these two distributions have statistical distance at most  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{0}: \left\{ \begin{array}{l} r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left([-1,1]^{m \times w}\right)^{|\overline{\mathsf{sk}}|}, \mathsf{ct} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}};r), \forall i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}], \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}} = \mathsf{Eval'}(\mathsf{pk}, f_{i,j}, 0, \mathsf{ct}) \\ \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{\star}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}^{\star} = \mathsf{ReRand}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}; \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}) : \left(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}, \left(\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}^{\star}\right)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}]}\right) \\ \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{1}: \left\{ \begin{array}{l} r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left([-1,1]^{m \times w}\right)^{|\overline{\mathsf{sk}}|}, \mathsf{ct} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}; r), \forall i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}], \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{\star} \\ \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}^{\star} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^{\star}(\mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j}); \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}) \\ \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}^{\star} = \mathsf{Eval}_{\mathsf{rand}} \left(\mathsf{pk}, f_{i,j}, r, \overline{\mathsf{sk}}\right) : \left(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}, \left(\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} - \mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}^{\star}\right)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}]}\right) \\ \end{array} \right\}.$$

We design an inefficient simulator  $\mathcal{S}$  that given a tuple  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}, (\mathbf{r}_{i,j}, \mathsf{ct}_{i,j})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]})$ , simulates the adversary view in the XiO security experiment. That is, we show that when fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}^0_{\lambda}$ ,  $\mathcal{S}$  simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{b.0}_{\lambda}$ , whereas it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{b.1}_{\lambda}$  when fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}^1_{\lambda}$ .

Given  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}, (\mathbf{r}_{i,j}, \mathsf{ct}_{f_{i,j}}^{\star})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]})$ ,  $\mathcal{S}$  (inefficiently) recovers  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}}$  from  $\overline{\mathsf{pk}}$ ,  $\mathsf{sk}$  from  $\overline{\mathsf{pk}}$ , and the randomness r from  $\mathsf{ct}$  (more precisely  $\mathcal{S}$  samples some uniformly random  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}}$ ,  $\mathsf{sk}$ , r among those that match  $\overline{\mathsf{pk}}$ ,  $\mathsf{pk}$  and  $\mathsf{ct}$ ). It samples LHE.PubCoin  $\leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0,1\}^{n^{1-\varepsilon}\cdot|\overline{\mathsf{ct}}|}$ , and for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]$ , sets  $\mathsf{FHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_{i,j} = \mathbf{r}_{i,j}$ , and  $\mathsf{pp} = (\mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}, (\mathsf{FHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_{i,j})_{i,j})$ . It computes  $\mathsf{ct}_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\Pi_b)$ ,  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}}(\mathsf{sk})$ .

For all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2], \mathcal{S}$  computes the following:

- $\operatorname{ct}_{i,j} = \operatorname{Eval}'(\operatorname{pk}, C_{i,j}, b + 2\lambda, \operatorname{ct}_1) \in \{0, 1\}^w;$
- $\bullet \ \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{ct}_{i,j} \in \{0,1\}^w.$
- Compute  $\operatorname{ct}_i = (\operatorname{ct}_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}, \operatorname{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i} = (\operatorname{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}.$
- $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Eval}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_i, \mathsf{ct}_i \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i});$
- $\rho_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{SecHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i).$

The simulator sets  $\widetilde{\Pi}_b = (\mathsf{pk}, \overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, (\rho_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]})$ , and returns  $(\mathsf{pp}, \widetilde{\Pi_b})$ . It is clear from the description of the simulator  $\mathcal{S}$  that when the latter is fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^0$ , it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.0}$ , whereas it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.1}$  when fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^1$ .

{42}------------------------------------------------

•  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.2}$ : this experiment is the same as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.1}$ , except that instead of sampling LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub> as random strings, they are sampled as fresh LHE ciphertexts of random plaintexts, that is, of the form LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub>  $\leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{u}_i)$  for  $\mathbf{u}_i \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ . By density of the ciphertexts of  $\mathcal{LHE}$  Property 4.7, we have:

$$\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.1}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.2}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$$

•  $\underline{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.3}}$ : this experiment is the same as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.2}$ , except the ciphertexts  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i$  are generated as fresh noisy LHE encryptions of the messages  $\mathbf{m}_i = \mathsf{sk}^{\top}(\mathsf{ct}_i - \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i}) + \mathbf{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , and the LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub> are instead computed homomorphically by subtracting the LHE encryption of the message  $\widetilde{\mathbf{m}}_i = \mathsf{sk}^{\top}(\mathsf{ct}_i + \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$  from the fresh noisy encryption of  $\mathbf{m}_i$ . That is, for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ ,  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\mathsf{pk}}^{\star}(\mathbf{m}_i)$ , LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub> =  $\overline{\mathsf{Eval}}\left(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i, -\mathsf{ct}_i + \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i}\right)$ .

Note that it is possible to define this hybrid since  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i}$  remains exactly the same no matter what  $\mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_i$  is. This was not true in  $\mathcal{H}^{b.0}_{\lambda}$ , and we introduced  $\mathcal{H}^{b.1}_{\lambda}$  to break this dependency. We show that for all  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , we have:

$$\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.2}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.3}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}},$$

using the weak circuit privacy property of  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$  (Property 4.6).

The latter states that for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , all  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}})$  in the support of  $\overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(1^{\lambda})$ , all vectors  $\mathbf{x} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^w$  and in particular  $\mathbf{x} = \mathsf{sk} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^w$ , all  $\mathbf{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , all functions  $\mathbf{y}^i = (\mathbf{y}_1^i, \dots, \mathbf{y}_{\ell_2}^i) \in [-1, 1]^{w\ell_2}$  and in particular the vector  $\mathsf{ct}_i - \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i} \in [-1, 1]^{w\ell_2}$  defined previously for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ , the following distributions have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ :

$$\begin{split} \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{0} &= \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \overline{\operatorname{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\operatorname{Enc}}_{\overline{\operatorname{pk}}}(\operatorname{sk}), \forall i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], \widetilde{\operatorname{ct}}_{i} \leftarrow \overline{\operatorname{Enc}}_{\overline{\operatorname{pk}}}^{\star}(\mathbf{u}_{i}) \\ \overline{\operatorname{ct}}_{i} &= \overline{\operatorname{Eval}}(\overline{\operatorname{pk}}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}, \widetilde{\operatorname{ct}}_{i}, \operatorname{ct}_{i} - \operatorname{ct}'_{\operatorname{MSB},i}) : \left(\overline{\operatorname{pk}}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}, (\widetilde{\operatorname{ct}}_{i}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}_{i})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}\right) \right\} \\ \mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{1} &= \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \overline{\operatorname{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\operatorname{Enc}}_{\overline{\operatorname{pk}}}(\operatorname{sk}), \forall i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], \overline{\operatorname{ct}}_{i} \leftarrow \overline{\operatorname{Enc}}_{\overline{\operatorname{pk}}}^{\star}(\mathbf{m}_{i}) \\ \widetilde{\operatorname{ct}}_{i} &= \overline{\operatorname{Eval}}(\overline{\operatorname{pk}}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}_{i}, -\operatorname{ct}_{i} + \operatorname{ct}'_{\operatorname{MSB},i}) : \left(\overline{\operatorname{pk}}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}, (\widetilde{\operatorname{ct}}_{i}, \overline{\operatorname{ct}}_{i})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}\right) \right\}, \end{split}$$

where for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ ,  $\mathbf{m}_i = \mathsf{sk}^\top(\mathsf{ct}_i - \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i}) + \mathbf{u}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ .

We design an inefficient simulator  $\mathcal{S}$  that given a tuple  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, (\widetilde{\mathsf{ct}}_i, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]})$ , simulates the adversary view in the XiO security experiment. That is, we show that when fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}^0_{\lambda}$ ,  $\mathcal{S}$  simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{b.2}_{\lambda}$ , whereas it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{b.3}_{\lambda}$  when fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}^1_{\lambda}$ .

Given  $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, (\widetilde{\mathsf{ct}}_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]})$ ,  $\mathcal{S}$  (inefficiently) recovers  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}}$  from  $\overline{\mathsf{pk}}$ ,  $\mathsf{sk}$  from  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}$ ,  $\mathsf{pk}$  from  $\mathsf{sk}$  and  $\mathbf{u}_i$  from  $\widetilde{\mathsf{ct}}_i$  for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ . It generates  $\mathsf{ct}_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\Pi_b)$ ,  $r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left([-1,1]^{m \times w}\right)^{|\overline{\mathsf{sk}}|}$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_2 = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}};r)$ , for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ ,  $j \in [\ell_2]$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_{i,j} = \mathsf{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, C_{i,j}, b + 2\lambda, \mathsf{ct}_1)$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^\star \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^\star$ , where  $\mathcal{R}^\star$  denotes the noisy randomness space of  $\mathcal{FHE}_d$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{Enc}^\star_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j}); \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^\star)$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}} = \mathsf{Eval}_{\mathsf{rand}}(\mathsf{pk}, f_{i,j}, r, \overline{\mathsf{sk}})$ ,  $\mathsf{FHE.PubCoin}_{i,j} = \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^\star - \mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}}$ ,  $\rho_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{SecHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i)$ ,  $\mathsf{LHE.PubCoin}_i = \widetilde{\mathsf{ct}}_i$ .

It returns  $pp = ((LHE.PubCoin_i)_i, (FHE.PubCoin_{i,j})_{i,j})$  and  $\widetilde{\Pi}_b = (pk, \overline{pk}, ct_1, ct_2, \overline{ct}, (\rho_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]})$ . It is clear from the description of the simulator S that when the latter is fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^0$ , it simulates  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.2}$ , whereas it simulates  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.3}$  when fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^1$ .

•  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}$ : it is the same experiment as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.3}$ , except the hints  $\rho_i$  for  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$  are computed using

{43}------------------------------------------------

 $\overline{\mathsf{PubHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, r_i)$ , where  $r_i$  denotes the randomness used to produce the ciphertext  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i$ ; instead of  $\overline{\mathsf{SecHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i)$ . By Property 4.4 of the LHE, we have  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.3}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . Note that in the experiment  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}$ , we no longer use the LHE secret key  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}}$ .

•  $\underline{\mathcal{H}}_{\lambda}^{b.5}$ : it is the same experiment as  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}$ , except that the ciphertexts  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i$  are generated as a fresh encryption of a message  $\mathbf{m}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$  of the form  $(m_{i,1},\ldots,m_{i,\ell_2})$  where for all  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , we have  $m_{i,j} = B2^{2\lambda} \cdot \Pi_{i,j}^b + \mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Recall that  $\mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}) = u_{i,j} \mod B2^{2\lambda} - B2^{2\lambda}/2 \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . This is instead of having  $m_{i,j} = \mathsf{sk}^\top (\mathsf{ct}_{i,j} + \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}) + u_{i,j} = B2^{2\lambda} \cdot \Pi_{i,j}^b + \mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}) + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ , where  $\mathsf{noise}_{i,j} = \mathbf{e}^\top \mathbf{r}_{C_{i,j}} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$  and  $\mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i} = \mathbf{e}^\top \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^\star \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{C_{i,j}}$  is the randomness obtained when evaluating the circuit  $C_{i,j}$  on the FHE ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^\star \leftarrow_\mathsf{R} \mathcal{R}^\star$ , and  $\mathbf{e} \leftarrow \chi^m$  is used to generate  $\mathsf{pk}$ .

Note that  $\mathsf{noise}_{i,j}$  and  $\mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i}$  are deterministic functions of  $\mathsf{pk}$ ,  $\mathsf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}$  and the randomness  $r \in ([-1,1]^{m \times w})^s$  used to produce  $\mathsf{ct}_1$ . In particular, they are independent of  $\mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j})$ .

We show that  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.3}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . To do so, for all  $\lambda\in\mathbb{N}$ , we exhibit two distributions  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^0$  and  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^1$ , together with a (possibly inefficient) simulator  $\mathcal{S}$ , such that (1)  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^0$  and  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^1$  have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ , and (2) for all  $\beta\in\{0,1\}$ , when fed with an input from distribution  $\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{\beta}$ ,  $\mathcal{S}$  produces the adversary view as in the experiment  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4+\beta}$ .

The distributions are defined as follows (the differences are highlighted in red):

$$\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{0} = \left\{ \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(\mathsf{crs}), r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left([-1, 1]^{m \times w}\right)^{s}, \forall i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}], \mathbf{r}_{i, j}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{\star} \\ \gamma_{i, j} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -B2^{2\lambda}/2 + 1, B2^{2\lambda}/2 \right] : \left(\mathsf{pk}, r, \left(\gamma_{i, j}, \mathbf{r}_{i, j}^{\star}\right)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}]}\right) \end{array} \right\}$$

$$\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{1} = \left\{ \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(\mathsf{crs}), r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left([-1,1]^{m \times w}\right)^{s}, \forall i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}], \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{\star} \\[0.2cm] \gamma_{i,j} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left[ -B2^{2\lambda}/2 + 1, B2^{2\lambda}/2 \right] : \left( \mathsf{pk}, r, \left( \gamma_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}, \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \right)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_{2}]} \right) \end{array} \right\},$$

where  $\mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}$  are functions of  $\mathsf{pk}$ , r and  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}$  defined as below, namely,  $\mathsf{noise}_{i,j} = \mathbf{e}^{\top} \mathbf{r}_{C_{i,j}}$  and  $\mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathbf{e}^{\top} \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star}$ .

We show that these distributions have statistical distance  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ . The only difference is that in  $\mathcal{D}^1_{\lambda}$ , an extra noise  $\mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}$  is added to the random value  $s_{i,j}$ . This noise is small, indeed  $|\mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}| \leq B(2^{\lambda} + 1)$  (see the correctness section for more details). Moreover,  $\gamma_{i,j}$  is sampled uniformly at random over  $[-B2^{2\lambda}/2+1,B2^{2\lambda}/2]$ , independently of the other values output by the distributions. Thus, we can use the value  $\gamma_{i,j}$  to smudge the noise  $\mathsf{noise}_{i,j} + \mathsf{noise}_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j}$ . That is, by Lemma 2.2 (smudging), the statistical distance of the two distributions is  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

Now, we proceed to describe the simulator S. Given as input the tuple  $\left(\mathsf{pk}, r, (v_{i,j}, \mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]}\right)$ , the simulator (inefficiently) recovers  $\mathsf{sk}$  from  $\mathsf{pk}$ ,  $\mathsf{samples}$   $(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Gen}}(1^{\lambda})$ , generates  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathsf{sk})$ ,

 $\mathsf{ct}_1 = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\Pi_b; r)$ . It samples  $r' \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \left( [-1, 1]^{m \times w} \right)^{|\mathsf{sk}|}$ , computes  $\mathsf{ct}_2 = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}} \left( \overline{\mathsf{sk}}; r' \right)$ . For all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]$ , samples  $\omega_{i,j} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{N/(2^{2\lambda}B)}$ , and sets  $m_{i,j} = B2^{2\lambda} \cdot \Pi_{i,j}^b + v_{i,j} + \omega_{i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

Note that  $(\gamma_{i,j}, \omega_{i,j})$  is identically distributed to  $(\mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}), \mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j}))$  for  $u_{i,j} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

It sets  $\mathbf{m}_i = (m_{i,1}, \dots, m_{i,\ell_2}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\ell_2}$ , samples  $r_i \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \overline{\mathcal{R}}$ , where  $\overline{\mathcal{R}}$  denotes the randomness space of  $\overline{\mathsf{Enc}}$ , computes  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{m}_i; r_i)$  and  $\rho_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{PubHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, r_i)$ . It computes  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{Enc}^{\star}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\omega_{i,j}; \mathbf{r}^{\star}_{i,j})$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_{i,j} = \mathsf{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, C_{i,j}, b + 2\lambda, \mathsf{ct}_1)$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_i = (\mathsf{ct}_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0, 1\}^{w\ell_2}$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i} = (\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0, 1\}^{w\ell_2}$ , and  $\mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Eval}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i, -\mathsf{ct}_i + \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i})$ . It computes  $\mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}} = \mathsf{Eval}_{\mathsf{rand}}(\mathsf{pk}, f_{i,j}, \mathsf{ct}_2)$  where the functions  $f_{i,j}$  are defined as before, and sets  $\mathsf{FHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_{i,j} = \mathbf{r}^{\star}_{i,j} - \mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^m$ .

{44}------------------------------------------------

It returns  $pp = (LHE.PubCoin_i, FHE.PubCoin_{i,j})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}$ , and  $\widetilde{\Pi}_b = (pk, \overline{pk}, ct_1, ct_2, \overline{ct}, (\rho_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]})$ . When  $\mathcal{S}$  is fed with an input distributed according to  $\mathcal{D}^0_{\lambda}$ , it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{b.4}_{\lambda}$ , whereas it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{b.5}_{\lambda}$  when fed with distribution  $\mathcal{D}^1_{\lambda}$ . Thus, we have:

$$\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$$

•  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c}\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ : To complete the proof, we show that  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is computationally indistinguishable from  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . These two ensembles are the same except the former obfuscates the program  $\Pi^{0}$ , whereas the latter obfuscates  $\Pi^{1}$ . Note that other than the encrypted key cycle, we never use the FHE secret key, and due to hybrid  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b.4}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , we no longer use the LHE secret key. The coins FHE.PubCoin exactly correspond to an SRL leakage on the FHE ciphertext  $\operatorname{ct}_{2}$  (and note that in the experiment we do know the output  $\alpha_{i,j}$  of the function  $f_{i,j}$  that is applied to the plaintexts encrypted in  $\operatorname{ct}_{1}$ ,  $\operatorname{ct}_{2}$ —namely, it is  $\operatorname{MSB}(u_{i,j})$  where  $u_{i,j}$  is a random element of  $\mathbb{Z}_{N}$  selected in the experiment, see Hybrid  $\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{b,2}$ ). Thus, (subexponential) indistinguishability of  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.5}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  follows from (subexponential) 2-circular SRL-security of  $\mathcal{FHE}_{d}$  and  $\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}$ .

Namely, for any nuPPT (resp. subexponential) distinguisher  $\mathcal{A}$ , we show there exists a nuPPT (resp. subexponential) reduction  $\mathcal{B}$  such that for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , we have:

$$\Pr\left[b \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0,1\}, (\mathsf{pp}, \widetilde{\Pi}^b) \leftarrow \mathcal{H}^{b.5}_{\lambda} : \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp}, \widetilde{\Pi}^b) = b\right] \leq \Pr\left[\mathsf{Exp}^{\mathcal{FHE}_d, \mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}}_{\lambda, \mathcal{B}} = 1\right] + 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)},$$

where the experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_{\lambda,\mathcal{B}}^{\mathcal{FHE}_d,\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}}$  is described in Definition 2.9.

We now proceed to describe the reduction  $\mathcal{B}$ . Given the public keys  $\mathsf{pk}$ ,  $\overline{\mathsf{pk}}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  sends the pair  $(\Pi^0,\Pi^1)$  to the 2-circular SRL security experiment, upon which it receives the ciphertexts  $\mathsf{ct} = (\mathsf{ct}_1\|\mathsf{ct}_2)$  and  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}$ , where  $\mathsf{ct}_1$  encrypts  $\Pi^0$  or  $\Pi^1$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_2$  encrypts  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}}$ , and  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}$  encrypts  $\mathsf{sk}$ . It samples  $u_{i,j} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_N$  for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]$ , and generates the following:

- Generation of pp:
  - To generate LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub>:
    - \* It samples  $r_i \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \overline{\mathcal{R}}$ , where  $\overline{\mathcal{R}}$  denotes the randomness space of  $\overline{\mathsf{Enc}}$ , and computes  $\overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i = \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathbf{m}_i; r_i)$ , where for all  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , the j'th coordinate of  $\mathbf{m}_i$  is of the form:  $m_{i,j} = B2^{2\lambda} \cdot \Pi_{i,j}^b + \mathsf{LSB}(u_{i,j}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ . Note that this does not require to know the bit b, since  $\Pi_{i,j}^0 = \Pi_{i,j}^1$  for all  $i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]$ ,  $j \in [\ell_2]$ , because the programs  $\Pi^0$  and  $\Pi^1$  are functionally equivalent.
    - \* It computes  $\rho_i \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{PubHint}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, r_i)$ .
    - \* It computes  $\mathsf{ct}_{i,j} = \mathsf{Eval}'(\mathsf{pk}, C_{i,j}, b + 2\lambda, \mathsf{ct}_1)$ .
    - \* Then, it queries its  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}$  oracle, to obtain a fresh, extra noisy encryption  $\mathsf{Enc}^{\star}_{\mathsf{pk}}(0;\mathbf{r}^{\star}_{i,j})$ . It leaves the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}$  pending.
    - \* It adds the vector  $(\mathbf{0}, \mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j})) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$  to the vector whose binary decomposition is  $\mathsf{Enc}^{\star}_{\mathsf{pk}}(0; \mathbf{r}^{\star}_{i,j})$ , which yields a vector  $\mathsf{ct}^{\star}_{i,j} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\kappa+1}$  whose binary decomposition is  $\mathsf{Enc}^{\star}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j}); \mathbf{r}^{\star}_{i,j})$ . Then, it computes  $\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j} = \mathsf{BD}(\mathsf{ct}^{\star}_{i,j}) \in \{0,1\}^w$ .
    - \* It computes  $\mathsf{ct}_i = (\mathsf{ct}_{i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2} \text{ and } \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i} = (\mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i,j})_{j \in [\ell_2]} \in \{0,1\}^{w\ell_2}.$
    - \* Finally, it computes LHE.PubCoin<sub>i</sub> =  $\overline{\mathsf{Eval}}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}_i, -\mathsf{ct}_i \mathsf{ct}'_{\mathsf{MSB},i})$ .
  - To generate FHE.PubCoin<sub>i,j</sub>: it answers the pending oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}$  with the function  $f_{i,j}$  and the value  $\alpha = \mathsf{MSB}(u_{i,j})$ . With probability  $1 2^{\Omega(\lambda)}$  over the random coins used to produce The oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}$  returns the leakage  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}} \in \mathcal{R}^{\star}$ . The reduction sets FHE.PubCoin<sub>i,j</sub> =  $\mathbf{r}_{i,j}^{\star} \mathbf{r}_{f_{i,j}}$ .

{45}------------------------------------------------

 $\text{It sets pp} = \left( (\mathsf{LHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]}, (\mathsf{FHE}.\mathsf{PubCoin}_{i,j})_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}], j \in [\ell_2]} \right).$ 

• Generation of  $\widetilde{\Pi}$ : it sets  $(pk, \overline{pk}, \overline{ct}, ct, (\rho_i)_{i \in [n^{1-\varepsilon}]})$  computed as described above.

The reduction  $\mathcal{B}$  sends  $(\mathsf{pp},\widetilde{\Pi})$  to the distinguisher  $\mathcal{A}$ , which outputs a bit b'. Finally,  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs the bit b'. When  $\mathsf{ct}_1$  encrypts  $\Pi^0$ , the reduction simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{0.5}_{\lambda}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ , whereas it simulates the experiment  $\mathcal{H}^{1.5}_{\lambda}$  when  $\mathsf{ct}_1$  encrypts  $\Pi^1$ . Thus, we have  $\Pr\left[\mathsf{Exp}_{\lambda,\mathcal{B}}^{\mathcal{FHE}_d,\mathcal{LHE}_{b,n,\varepsilon}} = 1\right] \geq \Pr\left[b \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \{0,1\}, (\mathsf{pp},\widetilde{\Pi}^b) \leftarrow \mathcal{H}^{b.5}_{\lambda} : \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp},\widetilde{\Pi}^b) = b\right]$ . Overall, we have shown that:

$$\{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.1}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.2}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.3}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.4}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{0.5}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.5}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.4}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.3}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_s \{\mathcal{H}_{\lambda}^{1.1}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$$

### <span id="page-45-0"></span>5.4 Instantiation with Packed-Regev LHE

We now state the results when instantiating our modular XiO construction with the Packed-Regev LHE, presented in Section 4.2. This construction is parameterized by polynomials  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ , and it is denoted by P-Regev $_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$ .

By combining Theorem 4.3 (i.e. security of P-Regev<sub> $\ell_1,\ell_2$ </sub> for all polynomials  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$  under LWE) and Theorem 3.5 (i.e. SRL-security of the GSW<sub> $\delta$ </sub> for all polynomials  $\delta$  under LWE), we get:

<span id="page-45-1"></span>**Lemma 5.1.** Assume the (subexponential) the LWE assumption holds. Assume further that for all polynomials  $\delta$ ,  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ ,  $2\mathsf{CIRC}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}}$  holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{P}\text{-Regev}_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$ . Then, for all polynomials  $\delta$ ,  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ , (subexponential) 2-circular SRL security holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{P}\text{-Regev}_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$ .

By combining Lemma 5.1 above with Theorem 4.2, which states that for all polynomials  $\ell_1$ , there exists a polynomial h such that for all polynomials  $\ell_2$ , P-Regev $_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$  is an  $(\ell_1,\ell_2,h,\alpha)$ -hintable packed LHE with  $\alpha(\lambda) = \lambda + 1$ , together with Theorem 5.2, we get:

<span id="page-45-2"></span>**Theorem 5.3.** Assume the (subexponential) LWE assumption holds. Assume further that for all polynomials  $\delta$ ,  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ , the (subexponential)  $2\mathsf{CIRC}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}}$  conjecture holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{P}\text{-Regev}_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$ . Then (subexponentially-secure)  $Xi\mathcal{O}$  for  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{log}}/\mathsf{poly}$  exists.

Finally, combining Theorem 5.3 with Theorem 2.4 (i.e.,  $i\mathcal{O}$  from  $Xi\mathcal{O}$  and LWE) we get our main theorem:

**Theorem 5.4.** Assume the subexponential LWE assumption holds. Assume further that for all polynomials  $\delta$ ,  $\ell_1$  and  $\ell_2$ , the subexponential  $2\mathsf{CIRC}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}}$  conjecture holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{P}\text{-Regev}_{\ell_1,\ell_2}$ . Then subexponentially-secure  $i\mathcal{O}$  for  $\mathsf{P}/\mathsf{poly}$  exists.

### Acknowledgments

We wish to thank Hoeteck Wee and Daniel Wichs for their insightful feedback on a previous eprint version of this paper. In particular, they encouraged us to present a game-based definition of SRL security (as opposed to the indistinguishability based definition we presented in our earlier draft), and to clarify differences between circular SRL-security and "plain" circular security.
