# A XiO from the 2-circular SRL Security of the GSW FHE and the DJ LHE

## <span id="page-51-12"></span>A.1 Hintable LHE from DCR

We consider the Damg˚ard Jurik (DJ) Linearly Homomorphic Encryption scheme from [\[DJ01\]](#page-48-10), which generalizes Paillier's encryption scheme [\[Pai99\]](#page-51-13) to larger message spaces, whose security relies on the Decisional Composite Residuosity (DCR) assumption. This scheme is not needed for our main result, 

{52}------------------------------------------------

but serves as a good warm-up for understanding the notion of a hintable packed LHE (and leads to our simplest construction of an  $Xi\mathcal{O}$ ). As mentionned in the introduction, BDGM already showed that the DJ scheme is a hintable LHE; since our notion of a hintable LHE is somewhat different, for completeness, we here include the standard proof. We start by recalling the DCR assumption under which the DJ scheme is proven secure.

<span id="page-52-0"></span>**Definition A.1** (Decisional Composite Residuosity (DCR) assumption [Pai99]). We say that security of the DCR assumption holds if there exists a PPT algorithm RSAsample that on input a security parameter  $\lambda$ , outputs a pair  $(N, \phi(N))$  where N is a  $2\lambda$ -bits integer,  $\phi$  denotes Euler's totient function; such that  $\gcd(\phi(N), N) = 1$  and such that for all polynomial  $\zeta(\cdot)$ , the following ensembles are computationally indistinguishable:

$$\begin{split} &\{\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{0}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} = \left\{(N, \phi(N)) \leftarrow \mathsf{RSAsample}(1^{\lambda}); r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M} : r^{N^{\zeta}(\lambda)} \in \mathbb{Z}_{N^{\zeta(\lambda)+1}}\right\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \\ &\{\mathcal{D}_{\lambda}^{0}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} = \left\{(N, \phi(N)) \leftarrow \mathsf{RSAsample}(1^{\lambda}); u \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{N^{\zeta(\lambda)+1}} : u \in \mathbb{Z}_{N^{\zeta(\lambda)+1}}\right\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \end{split}$$

We say the DCR assumption holds if 1-security of the LWE assumption holds, and that the subexponential DCR assumption holds if there exists  $\varepsilon > 0$  such that  $2^{\lambda^{\varepsilon}}$ -security of the DCR assumptions holds.

As explained in [DJ01] in further details, the algorithm RSAsample( $1^{\lambda}$ ) samples two safe primes p, q of  $\lambda$  bits each, and compute the RSA modulus N = pq.

We will show how the DJ encryption scheme satisfies our notion of a hintable packed LHE (actually even without any packing):

<span id="page-52-1"></span>**Theorem A.2.** Assume (subexponential) security of the DCR assumption. Then, for every polynomial  $\ell_1$ , there exists a (subexponentially) secure  $(\ell_1, \ell_2, h, \alpha)$ -hintable packed LHE, where  $h(\lambda) = 2\lambda$ ,  $\ell_2(\lambda) = 1$ , and  $\alpha(\lambda) = 0$ .

#### A.1.1 The DJ scheme

Given a polynomial  $\ell_1(\cdot)$ , we recall the LHE from [DJ01] when operating on plaintext of size  $\ell_1$  (recall that  $\ell_2 = 1$  so there is no packing). That is, the scheme is parameterized by a polynomial  $\ell_1$ , and we call it  $\mathrm{DJ}_{\ell_1}$ . For this scheme, the hint is simply the randomness used to encrypt a message, and noisy and normal encryptions behave in the same way:

## • $\mathsf{CRSgen}(1^{\lambda})$ :

It simply outputs  $crs = 1^{\lambda}$ , i.e. there is no proper crs for that scheme.

#### • Gen(crs):

Given  $\operatorname{crs} = 1^{\lambda}$ , it uses the sampling algorithm from Definition A.1,  $(M, \phi(M)) \leftarrow \operatorname{RSAsample}(1^{\lambda})$ , where  $M \in \mathbb{N}$  is a  $2\lambda$ -bit modulus,  $\phi$  denotes Euler's totient function, and we have  $\gcd(\phi(M), M) = 1$ . Then it chooses a polynomial  $\zeta(\cdot)$  such that  $2^{\ell_1(\lambda)+2\lambda} > N \geq 2^{\ell_1(\lambda)}$ , where  $N = M^{\zeta(\lambda)}$ . For simplicity of the notations, we write  $\zeta = \zeta(\lambda)$ . It sets  $\operatorname{pk} = (N, \zeta)$ ,  $\operatorname{sk} = \operatorname{td} = \phi(M)$  and outputs  $(\operatorname{pk}, \operatorname{sk}, \operatorname{td})$ . The plaintext space is  $\mathbb{Z}_N = \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta}}$ . The randomness space for  $\operatorname{Enc}$  is  $\mathbb{Z}_M^*$ , the ciphertext space is  $\mathbb{Z}_M^*$ , and the function space is  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ , that is t = N.

### • $Enc_{pk}(\mathbf{x})$ :

Given the public pk, a vector  $\mathbf{x} \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\nu}$ , for all  $i \in [\nu]$ , it samples  $r_i \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_M^*$  and compute  $\mathsf{ct}_i = r_i^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x_i} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ . It outputs the ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct} = (\mathsf{ct}_1, \dots, \mathsf{ct}_{\nu})$ .

{53}------------------------------------------------

## • $\mathsf{Enc}^{\star}_{\mathsf{pk}}(m)$ :

Given the public pk, a message  $m \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ , it samples  $r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_M^*$  and outputs the noisy ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^* = r^{M^\zeta} \cdot (1+M)^m \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ .

### • Eval( $pk, ct, ct^*, y$ ):

Given as input the public key pk, ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^{*\nu}$ , noisy ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^{\star} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^{*}$ , and a vector  $\mathbf{y} \in [-1,1]^{\nu}$ , it outputs the evaluated ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^{\star} \cdot \prod_{i \in [\nu]} \mathsf{ct}_{i}^{y_{i}} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^{*}$ , where  $\cdot$  denotes the integer multiplication in  $\mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^{*}$ .

### • SecHint(td, ct\*):

Given the secret key td and a noisy ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^\star \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ , it computes  $d = \mathsf{ct} \mod M$ . Since  $\gcd(M^\zeta, \phi(M)) = 1$ , it can compute  $M^{-\zeta} \in \mathbb{Z}$  such that  $M^\zeta \cdot M^{-\zeta} = 1 \mod \phi(M)$ . It outputs the hint  $d^{M^{-\zeta}} \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$ .

### • PubHint(pk, r):

Given the public key pk and some randomness  $r \in Z_M^*$ , it outputs the hint  $\rho = r$ .

## $\bullet \ \mathsf{Rec}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{ct}^\star,\rho) \colon$

Given the public key  $\mathsf{pk}$ , a noisy ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^*$ , and a hint  $\rho \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$ , it computes  $d = \mathsf{ct} \cdot r^{-M^{\zeta}} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ , where  $\rho^{-M^{\zeta}}$  is the inverse of  $\rho^{M^{\zeta}}$  in  $\mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ . Then, it applies Paillier's decryption recursively to obtain  $x \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta}}$ . It outputs  $x \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ .

## • $Dec_{sk}(ct^*)$ :

Given the secret key sk, a noisy ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^*$ , it runs  $\mathsf{Ext}(\mathsf{sk}, \mathsf{ct}^*)$  to recover the randomness  $r \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$ , then outputs  $\mathsf{Rec}(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{ct}^*, r)$ .

The proof of Theorem A.2 follows from the propositions and theorem below (which demonstrate that DJ satisfies the desired properties of a hintable packed LHE, as well as security).

**Proposition 14** (Linear Homomorphism). The LHE presented above satisfies Property 4.2.

**Proof:** For all  $i \in [\nu]$ , let  $\mathsf{ct}_i$  be a ciphertext in the support of  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(x_i)$ , that is, of the form  $\mathsf{ct}_i = (r_i)^{M^\zeta} \cdot (1+M)^{x_i} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ , and let  $\mathsf{ct}^\star$  be a ciphertext in the support of  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^\star(x^\star)$ , that is, of the form  $\mathsf{ct}^\star = r^{M^\zeta} \cdot (1+M)^{x^\star} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ . For all  $\mathbf{y} \in \{0,1\}^\nu$ , the evaluated ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}}$  is of the form:  $\left(r\prod_{i\in[\nu]}r_i^{y_i}\right)^{M^\zeta} \cdot (1+M)^{x^\star+\sum_{i\in[\nu]}x_iy_i} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ , which is in the support of  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^\star(x^\star+\sum_{i\in[\nu]}x_iy_i)$ .  $\square$ 

<span id="page-53-0"></span>**Proposition 15** (0-approximate correctness of secret hints). The LHE presented above satisfies 0-approximate correctness, as defined in Property 4.3.

**Proof:** Let  $\mathsf{ct}^\star = r^{M^\zeta} \cdot (1+M)^{x^\star} \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ , where  $x^\star \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^\zeta}$  is the message and  $r \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$  is the randomness used to produce the ciphertext. We have  $\mathsf{ct}^\star \mod M = r^{M^\zeta \mod \phi(M)} \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$ . Since  $\gcd(\phi(M), M^\zeta) = 1$ , there is  $M^{-\zeta} \in \mathbb{Z}$  such that  $M^\zeta \cdot M^{-\zeta} = 1 \mod \phi(M)$ . Thus, the algorithm SecHint(td, ct) outputs  $r \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$ . That is, the hint output by SecHint is the randomness used to produce  $\mathsf{ct}^\star$ .

The algorithm  $\operatorname{Rec}(\operatorname{pk},\operatorname{ct}^\star,r)$  computes  $d=\operatorname{ct}^\star\cdot r^{-M^\zeta}=(1+M)^{x^\star}\in\mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$  where  $r^{-M^\zeta}$  is the inverse of  $r^{M^\zeta}$  in  $\mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}^*$ . Then it applies Paillier's decryption recursively to obtain  $x^\star\in\mathbb{Z}_{M^\zeta}$ . It outputs  $x^\star$ .

{54}------------------------------------------------

**Proposition 16** (Equivalence between public hints and secret hints). The LHE presented above satisfies Property 4.4.

**Proof:** As seen in the proof of Proposition 15, the hint recovered by SecHint given the trapdoor td and a ciphertext  $ct^*$  is the randomness r used by  $Enc^*$  to produce  $ct^*$ , which is also what PubHint(pk, r) outputs.

**Proposition 17** (0-approximate correctness). The LHE presented above satisfies 0-approximate correctness, as defined in Property 4.1.

**Proof:** This directly follows from the 0-approximate correctness of the secret hints (Property 4.3), since decryption first computes the hint using the secret key, then recovers the message using the hint.  $\Box$ 

**Proposition 18** (h-succinctness of hints). The LHE presented above satisfies  $h(\lambda) = 2\lambda$ -succinctness.

**Proof:** For all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , for all pairs  $(\mathsf{pk}, \mathsf{sk})$  in the support of  $\mathsf{Gen}(1^{\lambda})$  that define the message space  $\mathbb{Z}_N$ , for all  $x^* \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ , all ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}^*$  in the support of  $\mathsf{Enc}^*_{\mathsf{pk}}(x^*)$ , we have: all hints  $\rho$  in the support of  $\mathsf{SecHint}(\mathsf{sk}, \mathsf{ct}^*)$  are in  $\mathbb{Z}_M^*$ , where M is an RSA modulus of size at most  $2\lambda$  bits.

**Proposition 19** (Weak circuit privacy). The LHE presented above satisfies Property 4.6 (weak circuit privacy).

**Proof:** For any message  $\mathbf{x} = (x_1, \dots, x_{\nu}) \in \mathbb{Z}_N^{\nu}$ ,  $x^* \in \mathbb{Z}_N$ ,  $\mathbf{y} \in \{0, 1\}^{\nu}$ , we aim at proving that following distributions are identical:

$$\mathcal{D}_{0}: \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \forall i \in [\nu], r_{i} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M}^{*}, \mathsf{ct}_{i} = r_{i}^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x_{i}}, r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M}^{*}, \mathsf{ct}^{\star} = r^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x^{\star}} \\ \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}} = (r \prod_{i} r_{i}^{y_{i}})^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x^{\star}+\mathbf{x}^{\top}\mathbf{y}} : ((\mathsf{ct}_{i})_{i}, \mathsf{ct}^{\star}, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}}) \end{array} \right\}$$

$$\mathcal{D}_{1}: \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \forall i \in [\nu], r_{i} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M}^{*}, \mathsf{ct}_{i} = r_{i}^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x_{i}}, r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M}^{*}, \mathsf{ct}^{\star} = (r/\prod_{i} r_{i}^{y_{i}})^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x^{\star}} \\ \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}} = r^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^{x^{\star}+\mathbf{x}^{\top}\mathbf{y}} : ((\mathsf{ct}_{i})_{i}, \mathsf{ct}^{\star}, \mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{y}}) \end{array} \right\}.$$

This relies on the fact that for all  $i \in [\nu]$ , all  $r_i \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$ , all  $y_i \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^\zeta}$ , the following distributions are identical:  $\mathcal{D}_0' = \{r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_M^* : ((r_i)_i, r, r \cdot \prod_i r_i^{y_i})\}$  and  $\mathcal{D}_1' = \{r \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_M^* : ((r_i)_i, r/(\prod_i r_i^{y_i}), r)\}$ . The distribution  $\mathcal{D}_0'$  corresponds to  $\mathcal{D}_0$ , whereas  $\mathcal{D}_1'$  corresponds to  $\mathcal{D}_1$ .

**Proposition 20** (Density of the noisy ciphertexts). The LHE presented above satisfies Property 4.7 (density of the noisy ciphertexts).

**Proof:** One can sample a uniform random value  $u \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}$  from  $\lceil \log(M^{\zeta+1}) \rceil$  random bits. The random value  $u \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}$  can be written  $u = r^{M^{\zeta}} \cdot (1+M)^x$  where  $x \in \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta}}$  and  $r \in \mathbb{Z}_M^*$  with probability  $1 - \frac{\phi(N)}{N} > 1 - \frac{3}{2^{\lambda}}$  over the choice of  $u \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathbb{Z}_{M^{\zeta+1}}$ .

<span id="page-54-1"></span>**Theorem A.3** (Security [DJ01]). Assuming the (subexponential) DCR assumption, the DJ scheme is (subexponentially) secure.

### <span id="page-54-0"></span>A.2 Instantiation with DJ LHE

Now we instantiate the modular XiO construction described in Section 5.2 with the DJ LHE presented in Section A.1 that is parameterized by a polynomial  $\ell_1$ ; we denote it by DJ $_{\ell_1}$ . For all polynomials  $\delta$ , we denote by GSW $_{\delta}$  the GSW FHE scheme for depth  $\delta$  circuits.

By combining Theorem A.3 (i.e. security of  $\mathrm{DJ}_{\ell_1}$  for all polynomials  $\ell_1$  under DCR) and Theorem 3.5 (i.e. SRL-security of the  $\mathrm{GSW}_{\delta}$  for all polynomials  $\delta$  under LWE), we get:

{55}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-55-1"></span>**Lemma A.1.** Assume the (subexponential) DCR and the (subexponential) LWE assumptions hold. Assume further that for all polynomials  $\delta$  and  $\ell_1$ , the  $2\mathsf{CIRC}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}}$  assumption holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{DJ}_{\ell_1}$ . Then, for all polynomials  $\delta$  and  $\ell_1$ , (subexponential) 2-circular SRL security holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{DJ}_{\ell_1}$ .

By combining Lemma A.1 above with Theorem A.2, which states that for all polynomials  $\ell_1$ , DJ $_{\ell_1}$  is an  $(\ell_1, \ell_2, h, \alpha)$ -hintable packed LHE with  $\ell_2(\lambda) = 1$ ,  $h(\lambda) = 2\lambda$  and  $\alpha(\lambda) = 0$ , together with Theorem 5.2, we get:

<span id="page-55-2"></span>**Theorem A.4.** Assume the (subexponential) DCR and (subexponential) LWE assumptions hold. Assume further that for all polynomials  $\delta$ ,  $\ell_1$ , the  $2\mathsf{CIRC}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}}$  assumption holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{DJ}_{\ell_1}$ . Then (subexponentially-secure) XiO for  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{log}}/\mathsf{poly}$  exists.

Finally, combining Theorem A.4 with Theorem 2.4 (i.e.,  $i\mathcal{O}$  from  $Xi\mathcal{O}$  and LWE) yields:

**Theorem A.5.** Assume the subexponential DCR and subexponential LWE assumptions hold. Assume further that that for all polynomials  $\delta$  and  $\ell_1$  the  $2\mathsf{CIRC}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{SRL}}}$  holds w.r.t.  $\mathsf{GSW}_{\delta}$  and  $\mathsf{DJ}_{\ell_1}$ . Then subexponentially-secure  $i\mathcal{O}$  for  $\mathsf{P/poly}$  exists.

## <span id="page-55-0"></span>**B** Concrete Assumption

In Theorem 5.2, we show how to build XiO whose security relies on the 2-circular SRL security between the GSW FHE and an LHE with special properties. As mentioned in Section 3.1.3, it actually suffices to assume the following variant of 2-circular SRL security (that is weaker than that of definition Definition 3.3).

**Definition B.1** (One-shot SRL circular security). We say that one-shot SRL 2-circular security holds w.r.t. an FHE scheme  $\mathcal{FHE} = (\mathsf{CRSgen}, \mathsf{Gen}, \mathsf{Enc}, \mathsf{Enc}^*, \mathsf{Eval}', \mathsf{Eval}_{\mathsf{rand}}, \mathsf{Dec})$  that satisfies batch correctness (as per Definition 3.1) and randomness homomorphism (as per Definition 3.2) and a PKE scheme  $\overline{\mathcal{PKE}}$  if for all stateful nuPPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists some negligible function  $\mu(\cdot)$  such that for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_{\lambda,\mathcal{A}}^{\mathcal{FHE}} = 1] \leq 1/2 + \mu(\lambda)$ , where the experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_{\lambda,\mathcal{A}}^{\mathcal{FHE}}$  is defined as follows:

$$\mathsf{Exp}_{\lambda,\mathcal{A}}^{\mathcal{FHE}} = \left\{ \begin{array}{l} (\mathbf{m}^0,\mathbf{m}^1,q) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(1^{\lambda}), \overline{\mathsf{crs}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{CRSgen}}(1^{\lambda}) \\ (\overline{\mathsf{pk}},\overline{\mathsf{sk}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(\overline{\mathsf{crs}}), (\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{sk}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Gen}(\overline{\mathsf{pk}}), b \leftarrow \{0,1\} \\ \mathbf{r} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{|\overline{\mathsf{sk}}||\mathbf{m}^b|}, \mathsf{ct} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}||\mathbf{m}^b;\mathbf{r}), \overline{\mathsf{ct}} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{Enc}}_{\overline{\mathsf{pk}}}(\mathsf{sk}) \\ \forall i \in [q(\lambda)] : r_i^{\star} \leftarrow_{\mathsf{R}} \mathcal{R}^{\star}, \underline{\mathsf{ct}}_i = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{pk}}^{\star}(\mathbf{0};\mathbf{r}_i^{\star}) \\ (f_i,\alpha_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}\left(\mathsf{pk},\overline{\mathsf{pk}}, \mathtt{ct}, \overline{\mathsf{ct}}, (\underline{\mathsf{ct}}_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)]}\right) \\ \forall i \in [q(\lambda)], \mathbf{r}_{f_i} = \mathsf{Eval}_{\mathsf{rand}}(\mathsf{pk}, f_i, \mathbf{r}, \overline{\mathsf{sk}}||\mathbf{m}^b), \mathsf{leak}_i = \mathbf{r}_i^{\star} - \mathbf{r}_{f_i} \\ b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}\left((\mathsf{leak}_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)]}\right) \\ \mathcal{R}eturn \ 1 \ if \ |\mathbf{m}^0| = |\mathbf{m}^1|, \ b' = b \ and \ for \ all \ i \in [q(\lambda)], \ f_i(\overline{\mathsf{sk}}||\mathbf{m}^b) = \alpha_i; \ \theta \ otherwise. \end{array} \right\}$$
